    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1181231-how-do-i-go-about-reading-the-book-i-d">How do I go about reading the book? I&#39;d appreciate someone answering :)</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1181231'><a id="like_count_community_question_1181231" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/1181231?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">15 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F35235302-this-is-going-to-hurt">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/1181231-how-do-i-go-about-reading-the-book-i-d">3 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1181231-how-do-i-go-about-reading-the-book-i-d">See all 6 answers</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/10478272-muna"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1564258514i/10478272._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/10478272-muna">Muna</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I recommend that you buy it or borrow it from the library and then pick a nice, comfortable spot and just start reading, don't stop. Don't stop until <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I recommend that you buy it or borrow it from the library and then pick a nice, comfortable spot and just start reading, don't stop. Don't stop until you've read a couple of pages. Then when you're at the end of an entry that captures your attention, stop. Stop in order to think and reflect on what you would do differently if you were in Adam's shoes? How would you react to certain patients? How would you handle certain situations? This is how I went about reading it. I also found that the best time to read it was when I wasn't massively busy with anything. That way, I was able to concentrate and enjoy the book more than I thought I would. Maybe you could try it and see if this method works for you too :) <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_3654659365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=1-star-reads">1-star-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3654659365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3222731860484141470">I once met Adam Kay, and he left a distinct negative impression on me.<br/><br/>He was performing at the theatre where I used to work. And I feel like I can write this now, I no longer work there so these words are not a reflection on the business but merely the words of a disgruntled former employee. So, Adam came on a busy Saturday night where we had sold all the seats. His name was popular, and people wanted to hear what he had to say. He and his manager approached me to tell me about their show, the v</span>
  <span id="freeText3222731860484141470" style="display:none">I once met Adam Kay, and he left a distinct negative impression on me.<br /><br />He was performing at the theatre where I used to work. And I feel like I can write this now, I no longer work there so these words are not a reflection on the business but merely the words of a disgruntled former employee. So, Adam came on a busy Saturday night where we had sold all the seats. His name was popular, and people wanted to hear what he had to say. He and his manager approached me to tell me about their show, the visiting companies would inform the front of house manger about the show’s running times and give details about the content of the performance. This was all standard stuff.<br /><br />Adam’s manager then told me that Adam had promised eight seats to some of his friends last minute. And whilst Adam skulked in the background, letting his manger do all the talking, she told me that if I didn’t find these eight seats for his friends they would pull the plug on us and not perform. And obviously this would have been disastrous for the theatre and its patrons. Me and my team had to magic up these eight seats in an already full auditorium. Not an easy task. And we could not turn any of our customers away who had already paid for their tickets. <br /><br />So, my review is getting a little bit personal, but it is still about the book and his work if you let me continue. Fifteen minutes into the show, one of the ushers walked out. She was absolutely horrified at the content of the performance. The case Adam was delivery to the audience, sent her back to a horrific childhood memory involving a close friend. Adam delivered the story with humour and mirth, making light of someone’s medical disaster. And from here I decided I must read his book to see what all the fuss is about and to make up my own mind, separate to the negative impression he had already made on me personally. <br /><br />After reading it, almost two years later, I can say only one positive thing: Adam can write well. He delivers the stories well, but here I question the ethics behind doing so. In all honesty, should we really be laughing at other people’s medical disasters? And should we really be selling them to make a cheap buck? <br /><br />I don’t think so.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3222731860484141470" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2105489101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2105489101" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1170391-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590218363p2/1170391.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2105489101?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/1170391-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=biographies-and-memoirs">biographies-and-memoirs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=medical-and-science">medical-and-science</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1170391-sara?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2105489101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3622179025296375318">I loved this. In part funny and heartwarming, yet also utterly heartbreaking and disillusioned. I think this strikes a particular cord with me at the moment as the author was an obs & gynae doctor, and I’ve recently spent time myself as an inpatient on such a ward. <br/><br/>This is the first book in a while where I’ve read passages out to my husband while laughing out loud one minute and then had to hold back tears the next. It’s a full on rollercoaster of emotions that also seems to very accurately desc</span>
  <span id="freeText3622179025296375318" style="display:none">I loved this. In part funny and heartwarming, yet also utterly heartbreaking and disillusioned. I think this strikes a particular cord with me at the moment as the author was an obs &amp; gynae doctor, and I’ve recently spent time myself as an inpatient on such a ward. <br /><br />This is the first book in a while where I’ve read passages out to my husband while laughing out loud one minute and then had to hold back tears the next. It’s a full on rollercoaster of emotions that also seems to very accurately describe what it’s like to work as front line staff for the NHS. I should know, I do it everyday too, and we all have our stories to tell that encompass the best and worst of British medical care. It’s one of my favourite things about the job, hearing stories from everyone about ‘that time a patient shoved a remote control up their rectum’ or ‘remember that night shift a woman faked passing out’. I think it’s what binds and bonds you all together. The camaraderie. Told with a liberal dose sarcasm and self deprecating humour, the author manages to walk that tightrope between friend, colleague and reliable narrator to a finely tuned ‘T’. <br /><br />My admiration for other healthcare professionals is limitless, and will continue to be so. It’s really the awful and gut wrenching stories interspersed throughout (especially the last chapters) that make you realise how much pressure and guilt our doctors are under. And for little pay might I add. Day after day, night after night they fight to provide the best level of care they can without succumbing to sleep deprivation, depression or worse. There’s a lot of emotion here, a lot of anger and sadness that’s so hard to see, yet is oh so common in the increasingly frequent demoralised NHS worker.<br /><br />It’s a very bittersweet read, that I devoured in one day, and I’m sorry it’s over. It’s one of the best memoirs of this kind I’ve read in a long time and I loved following Adam Kay on his journey through life as a junior doctor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3622179025296375318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2339899472" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2339899472" />
    <a title="Sonja Arlow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6449756-sonja-arlow"><img alt="Sonja Arlow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576564309p2/6449756.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2339899472?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sonja Arlow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sonja Arlow" href="/user/show/6449756-sonja-arlow">Sonja Arlow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=medicine">medicine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=memoirs-bio-s">memoirs-bio-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=2018-read">2018-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=recommended">recommended</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6449756-sonja-arlow?shelf=favourite-books">favourite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2339899472" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13395533262033216076">I am going to be in so much trouble when my sister finds out I gave this book to my niece as this is probably not a very appropriate book for a 17-year-old. But she is determined to become a doctor and she needs to know it’s not just about rockstar surgeries and making buckets of money. It is the most insane working hours, thankless work with crap pay.<br/><br/>The diary entries follow Adam’s ascend through the ranks, from a junior doctor to becoming a consultant, specialising in gynaecology or “brats and</span>
  <span id="freeText13395533262033216076" style="display:none">I am going to be in so much trouble when my sister finds out I gave this book to my niece as this is probably not a very appropriate book for a 17-year-old. But she is determined to become a doctor and she needs to know it’s not just about rockstar surgeries and making buckets of money. It is the most insane working hours, thankless work with crap pay.<br /><br />The diary entries follow Adam’s ascend through the ranks, from a junior doctor to becoming a consultant, specialising in gynaecology or “brats and twats” I learned more about giving birth than I ever EVER wanted to. The writing style is not geared towards making you feel a deep connection with Adam however towards the end my heart really went out to him and is the reason I rounded up to a full 4 stars.<br /><br />The format took a while to get used to as some diary entries were so short they felt like Doctor Doctor jokes, but once I got used to it I could not stop reading.<br /><br />This was really entertaining, in fact at times I had to literally wipe away tears of laughter. But there were a few stories where I felt the author went over the line, where someone should have told him to leave it out of this collection. These made up only about 10% of the book so it was easy to forgive. I also found the footnotes explaining medical procedures very interesting and not as intrusive as footnotes normally tend to be.<br /><br />But this was not just all laughs, there were quite a few very touching stories that brought me back to reality, this is not a book full of fictitious jokes, it’s a book full of real people with serious medical problems. <br /><br />The overall impression I was left with was how utterly grueling the process of becoming a doctor really is, how the NHS is setup to grind the doctors down even further, getting to know the human (warts and all) behind the white coat and how much a thank you from a patient means.<br /><br />If you have an interest in medical memoirs and want a good laugh, then give this a try.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13395533262033216076" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I highly recommend this book, and wish it could be dished out as prescribed reading (if you'll pardon the pun).</span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739688292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13704209186895105138">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/05/05/this-is-going-to-hurt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><b>Actual Rating : 3.5 stars</b><br/><br/> <i> “A great doctor must have a huge heart and a distended aorta through which pumps a vast lake of compassion and human kindness.” </i><br/><br/>🌟 Yet another non-fiction I am reviewing at my blog! Who am I???<br/>This book is special since it is an insight to the medical field. I read this as a medical student but I am reviewing it as a doctor now.<br/><br/>🌟 The book had a shaky start and I was not impressed which I actua</span>
  <span id="freeText13704209186895105138" style="display:none">This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/05/05/this-is-going-to-hurt/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><b>Actual Rating : 3.5 stars</b><br /><br /> <i> “A great doctor must have a huge heart and a distended aorta through which pumps a vast lake of compassion and human kindness.” </i><br /><br />🌟 Yet another non-fiction I am reviewing at my blog! Who am I???<br />This book is special since it is an insight to the medical field. I read this as a medical student but I am reviewing it as a doctor now.<br /><br />🌟 The book had a shaky start and I was not impressed which I actually foresaw. I just didn’t expect that the author’s style is for me from the start but things were going in the right direction and I was intrigued so I continued to give it a chance.<br /><br />🌟 I didn’t know that the author was a Gynecologist and funny coincidence is that I read this one while preparing for my Gyne exam. I am mentioning this because I want to point out that Adam was apparently an excellent doctor and that the book was scientifically very accurate.<br /><br />🌟 The humor may have made a difficult topic easier to approach but it was not always funny nor it was always appropriate. I just wish that the book had a more serious tone at some points.<br /><br />🌟 I like that this showed how doctors and the medical workers in general suffer, it showed how there is a problem with the system. What I am going to say is that we doctors are human!! It may sound stupid but really people do think of doctors as robots who should function on 100% all the time, not have any negative emotions!<br />When I got really sick earlier this year, the first response I was getting from like 99% of the people around me is “You are a doctor, you should not get sick”. I am pretty sure it is all in good spirits and meant as a kind of a joke but people really want that from us!<br /><br />🌟 I am ending with a quote that I loved and that sums our mission in life as doctors. I think Adam said it perfectly:<br /><br /> <i> “So I told them the truth: the hours are terrible, the pay is terrible, the conditions are terrible; you’re underappreciated, unsupported, disrespected and frequently physically endangered. But there’s no better job in the world.” </i><br /><br />🌟 Prescription: For all people in general and for medical workers specially. I already recommended this to my close friends/ colleagues!</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Johann (jobis89)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Johann (jobis89)" href="/user/show/50893023-johann-jobis89">Johann (jobis89)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2845852948" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17678530226984325034">“So I told them the truth: the hours are terrible, the pay is terrible, the conditions are terrible; you’re underappreciated, unsupported, disrespected and frequently physically endangered. But there’s no better job in the world.”<br/><br/>A first-hand account of life as a junior doctor in all its joy, pain, sacrifice and maddening bureaucracy.<br/><br/>A really eye-opening read that provides insight into what it's really like to work for the NHS. My mother has been a nurse for 30+ years and from her I know how har</span>
  <span id="freeText17678530226984325034" style="display:none">“So I told them the truth: the hours are terrible, the pay is terrible, the conditions are terrible; you’re underappreciated, unsupported, disrespected and frequently physically endangered. But there’s no better job in the world.”<br /><br />A first-hand account of life as a junior doctor in all its joy, pain, sacrifice and maddening bureaucracy.<br /><br />A really eye-opening read that provides insight into what it's really like to work for the NHS. My mother has been a nurse for 30+ years and from her I know how hard it can be, but this just makes me appreciate those on the frontline even more.<br /><br />At the same time, I have never laughed so much or so hard at a book before. The stories and encounters Kay describes are often absolutely hilarious. I was constantly retelling the stories to those around me, as so many left me flabbergasted and needing to discuss with someone!! I would recommend the audiobook in particular as Kay delivers the punchlines so perfectly.<br /><br />Then once you get to the devastating experience on a ward that caused Kay to reconsider his future... it becomes heartbreaking. We need more support for those who face such a tough job every single day, I know I myself couldn't do it. This book was fantastic. 4.5 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17678530226984325034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2321700493" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2321700493" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2321700493?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2321700493" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14008652060161524638">This is a non-fiction read all about the NHS and the way that the system works. It's told in a diary format from the years when Adam Kay was a junior doctor and was part of the system. We see how the NHS has been struggling as time goes on to keep up the standards and staff levels, and we see the strain it can take on a doctor. We also get to see the way that Adam Kay dealt with many of the tests on his own time and relationships.<br/><br/>However, at the heart of this story it's all about humour and anec</span>
  <span id="freeText14008652060161524638" style="display:none">This is a non-fiction read all about the NHS and the way that the system works. It's told in a diary format from the years when Adam Kay was a junior doctor and was part of the system. We see how the NHS has been struggling as time goes on to keep up the standards and staff levels, and we see the strain it can take on a doctor. We also get to see the way that Adam Kay dealt with many of the tests on his own time and relationships.<br /><br />However, at the heart of this story it's all about humour and anecdotes and we get a real look at some of the truly silly and down-right mad things that people do to end up in A &amp; E. We also get to follow some of the stories which were quite embarrassing/funny or down-right painful (hence the title) and I found there were plenty of LOL moments in the book.<br /><br />There's a bit of a shocking ending, and that topped this off as a 4.5*s read for me. I really would recommend this one, and I enjoyed it immensely! </span>
  <a data-text-id="14008652060161524638" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2237121817" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237121817" />
    <a title="Leo Robertson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson"><img alt="Leo Robertson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1571602096p2/7619789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237121817?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leo Robertson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leo Robertson" href="/user/show/7619789-leo-robertson">Leo Robertson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237121817" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1765720911758721340">Excellent!<br/><br/>Breezed through this one. The sense of humour worked well, balanced with the horrors of Kay's job.<br/><br/>An Xmas present from my sis. She said, "You won't regret quitting medicine after reading this."<br/><br/>She knows I don't, really, though reading this I wondered if I would.<br/><br/>I think people assume I regret quitting medicine more than I do, which is, not at all. It had "not for me" all over it, and I've never experienced such an immense relief since leaving. My body was like, "Yeees, shut this shit do</span>
  <span id="freeText1765720911758721340" style="display:none">Excellent!<br /><br />Breezed through this one. The sense of humour worked well, balanced with the horrors of Kay's job.<br /><br />An Xmas present from my sis. She said, "You won't regret quitting medicine after reading this."<br /><br />She knows I don't, really, though reading this I wondered if I would.<br /><br />I think people assume I regret quitting medicine more than I do, which is, not at all. It had "not for me" all over it, and I've never experienced such an immense relief since leaving. My body was like, "Yeees, shut this shit down! Let's do anything else with the next... everything of our life!"<br />I made it a year and a half at St Andrews then switched to Chemical Engineering at Strathclyde, spending the intervening months folding schoolwear in a shop so I knew that anything at uni would be worth it eventually.<br />If this is even the first time you're reading that I ever studied medicine, it's because while I value your literary opinion immensely, I don't wake up giving a fuck how clever you think I am! (Okay it does come up in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25664171.Saxual_Healing" title="Saxual Healing by Billy Medicine" rel="nofollow noopener">Saxual Healing</a>, but it was relevant. A bit ;) )<br />A friend asked me about it when I met him in Greece this summer. I said, "It was never something I was supposed to be, so I don't think about it at all."<br />Maybe an equivalent is, "Was it difficult coming out?" Maybe, but it was less tough than staying in.<br />Anyway, I met some other people on that holiday, and it clicked.<br />"So you live in Norway," a man said. "What was Norway before they had oil? They were farmers! Fishermen! You know, we here in Greece are hoping to discover new oil reserves. And as a banker I work with many of the same companies as you anyway."<br />"Sure, sure," I said.<br />Why say, "Despite your weird attempted 'historical own', the guys I work with sure don't catch their own fish anymore!" or, "That stable oil price will help you guys secure energy independence after your exploration efforts definitely lead to reserves. Oil is the, uh, future..." I didn't engage, though. I was on holiday and didn't know the guy. (And I also wasn't drunk.)<br /><br />No one SHOULD have to justify themselves to others, but that's not how most people let the world work. Kay isn't bothering to justify himself and openly pokes fun at the idea that anyone could pick a suitable career at a young age, or that the criteria for acceptance for careers even make sense. But this is mainly a clarion call to action against the current conditions for junior doctors and perhaps a deeply reassuring text to those people who feel inadequate because they're not doctors.<br /><br />Wow what a sacrifice it is. I sure wasn't able to make it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1765720911758721340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer7378382846335151222">I'm supposed to be taking a break from social media right now, so I'll just say this: I feel better, more whole, more comforted, and more hopeful after reading this book. It's visceral, funny, and so poignant; what a memoir should be, real commentary on real life.   <span id="freeText7378382846335151222" style="display:none">I'm supposed to be taking a break from social media right now, so I'll just say this: I feel better, more whole, more comforted, and more hopeful after reading this book. It's visceral, funny, and so poignant; what a memoir should be, real commentary on real life. It's unpretentious, as if Adam Kay had come round for a chat and we got to talking about his time as a junior doctor. It's heartbreaking, a love letter to the people who make the NHS such a precious institution, and a retort to those who have bruised it. <br /><br />This is what a memoir should be. An elegy, a time capsule. It's a look at a life we so rarely see, but that we should all work to better understand. One of the best books I've read in a long time. <br /><br />Thanks, Adam. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8378502-barney?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8378502-barney?shelf=uk">uk</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8378502-barney?shelf=memoiries">memoiries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8378502-barney?shelf=nowadays">nowadays</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8378502-barney?shelf=z-atlas-uk">z-atlas-uk</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2608694598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14223991860226826312">I was expecting I'd enjoy this book but I ended up really disliking it. It starts off well with a few funny anecdotes but after a while I realised a lot of them are at the expense of the patient themselves. Yes I am the fun police, and I know humour is a way of coping, but there's something about the thought of a group of doctors chuckling about the time a dementia patient sexually assaulted another patient - and then a group of readers reading that and also chuckling - which doesn't sit well wi</span>
  <span id="freeText14223991860226826312" style="display:none">I was expecting I'd enjoy this book but I ended up really disliking it. It starts off well with a few funny anecdotes but after a while I realised a lot of them are at the expense of the patient themselves. Yes I am the fun police, and I know humour is a way of coping, but there's something about the thought of a group of doctors chuckling about the time a dementia patient sexually assaulted another patient - and then a group of readers reading that and also chuckling - which doesn't sit well with me.<br /><br />Also we can all agree that doctors deserve absolutely every penny they get and are entitled to far more than they're being paid currently. But there's nothing like someone pre-financial crash describing themselves as poor while also having just bought an apartment and a trip to the Mauritius which just aaaargh really gets under my skin.<br /><br />I couldn't finish the book in the end. I was about half way through and fading fast, only to come across an vignette about the doctor being called in to deliver a new-born 'mid-wank', which ends with him completing the procedure "still erect". It was genuinely the most horrifying sentence I have ever read.<br /><br />So yeah, 2 stars but mostly because (even though the book isn't really political itself) its popularity in the UK has contributed to conversations about how hard junior doctors work and how valuable their contributions are to the NHS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14223991860226826312" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2251899340" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2251899340" />
    <a title="Kate~Bibliophile Book Club" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9841866-kate-bibliophile-book-club"><img alt="Kate~Bibliophile Book Club" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582131478p2/9841866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2251899340?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kate~Bibliophile Book Club" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kate~Bibliophile Book Club" href="/user/show/9841866-kate-bibliophile-book-club">Kate~Bibliophile Book Club</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2251899340" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12115214846848181263">Not being in the UK, I can’t pass comment on the NHS or any of that, but I had seen plenty of chat about Adam’s book so I loaned it from the library to see what it was like. I am a fan of medical memoirs, so it was right up my street.<br/><br/>Adam writes with wit and humour, and even in the worst of situations this levity really makes a difference to the narrative. Doctors see people on the worst days of their lives, but we also see them on the worst days of theirs, even if we don’t realise it. We don’t </span>
  <span id="freeText12115214846848181263" style="display:none">Not being in the UK, I can’t pass comment on the NHS or any of that, but I had seen plenty of chat about Adam’s book so I loaned it from the library to see what it was like. I am a fan of medical memoirs, so it was right up my street.<br /><br />Adam writes with wit and humour, and even in the worst of situations this levity really makes a difference to the narrative. Doctors see people on the worst days of their lives, but we also see them on the worst days of theirs, even if we don’t realise it. We don’t know what they are going through, but Adam has given an insightful look into his life as a Junior Doctor and just how much it impacted him.<br /><br />I think what I enjoyed the most was the almost conversational aspect of the book. It’s written in diary entries from his time in hospitals, so they are often brief, but some of the entries are very powerful. Others really made me feel for him as his own personal life suffered at the hands of working absolutely crazy hours and nobody could understand why he was missing important events outside of work.<br /><br />I really enjoyed This Is Going To Hurt, even though enjoy seems like the wrong word considering the subject matter, but you know what I mean. Adam Kay has a way with words, and it made this a really easy read. Tough subjects obviously, but he made it more relatable with his affable writing manner.<br /><br />If you enjoy glimpse into the medical profession, and a little humour with your non-fiction the you should most certainly add this one to your list!<br /><br />Recommended!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12115214846848181263" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2516785250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2516785250" />
    <a title="GTF" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66513638-gtf"><img alt="GTF" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594722618p2/66513638.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2516785250?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="GTF" class="user" itemprop="url" name="GTF" href="/user/show/66513638-gtf">GTF</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2516785250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13443831594177390168">'This Is Going To Hurt" is a brilliant memoir of Adam Kay's career as a junior doctor. The book spares no detail with regard to every aspect of the job; it contains some very graphic accounts of unusual injuries and illnesses that he came across during his time in medicine, and it also details what it's really like to work for the UK's healthcare system. <br/><br/>In addition to its plethora of explicit details, Kay clears up a lot of the misconceptions that people tend to have about doctors, such as doct</span>
  <span id="freeText13443831594177390168" style="display:none">'This Is Going To Hurt" is a brilliant memoir of Adam Kay's career as a junior doctor. The book spares no detail with regard to every aspect of the job; it contains some very graphic accounts of unusual injuries and illnesses that he came across during his time in medicine, and it also details what it's really like to work for the UK's healthcare system. <br /><br />In addition to its plethora of explicit details, Kay clears up a lot of the misconceptions that people tend to have about doctors, such as doctors being excellent problem solvers, when in fact they are often just following procedures, and junior doctors earning hefty salaries, when in fact they are being paid less than minimum wage for years. <br /><br />"This Is Going to Hurt" is an interesting fusion of misery and humor. Although Kay didn't feel human anymore towards the end of his career in medicine, he still managed to see the funny side to some of his experiences in his grueling medical career.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13443831594177390168" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2201704991?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/10887793-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2201704991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13964347927474542399">This is the second book I read this year that I wish I had written (and, had I kept a diary, I probably could have - except the horrific penis-related injury I treated was not a de-gloving, but a fracture).<br/><br/>I'm a *junior* doctor, and his stories of life, death and everything in between just sound so reassuringly familiar. It's kinda nice to know that somebody else has been there, done that, got the T-shirt and got it stained by blood almost immediately. Relationship breakdown? Check. Missing out </span>
  <span id="freeText13964347927474542399" style="display:none">This is the second book I read this year that I wish I had written (and, had I kept a diary, I probably could have - except the horrific penis-related injury I treated was not a de-gloving, but a fracture).<br /><br />I'm a *junior* doctor, and his stories of life, death and everything in between just sound so reassuringly familiar. It's kinda nice to know that somebody else has been there, done that, got the T-shirt and got it stained by blood almost immediately. Relationship breakdown? Check. Missing out on weddings/birthday parties/funerals because you had to be in work? Check. Developing a scathing, sarcastic sense of humour in order to deal with the death, tragedy and pain that constantly surrounds you? Also check.<br /><br />For those who are not medical professionals, I would highly recommend reading it. It sheds a light on a reality that some might not know exists: what goes on behind the scenes and what happens to your doctor on a day-to-day basis (spoiler alert: it ain't all good). And, honestly, we probably need more people to read it if we want to save the NHS.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13964347927474542399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2391107852" />
    <a title="Anni" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17465866-anni"><img alt="Anni" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601464869p2/17465866.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2391107852?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anni" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anni" href="/user/show/17465866-anni">Anni</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2391107852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2335549657554641761">The Best Medicine<br/><br/>Well, you may not die laughing, but I was certainly in stitches and convulsed with hysterics, not to mention emotionally distraught, reading this diary of a junior doctor‘s training in the NHS. Apart from the side-splitting humour, it is an excoriating account of the manifold administration deficiencies throughout the National Health Service, once the jewel in the crown of Britain’s welfare society. <br/>The author decided to specialise in ‘obs & gynae’ (known in the medical world as</span>
  <span id="freeText2335549657554641761" style="display:none">The Best Medicine<br /><br />Well, you may not die laughing, but I was certainly in stitches and convulsed with hysterics, not to mention emotionally distraught, reading this diary of a junior doctor‘s training in the NHS. Apart from the side-splitting humour, it is an excoriating account of the manifold administration deficiencies throughout the National Health Service, once the jewel in the crown of Britain’s welfare society. <br />The author decided to specialise in ‘obs &amp; gynae’ (known in the medical world as ‘brats and - something I can't repeat here beginning with ‘t’) because you end up with twice as many patients, unlike in geriatrics, and it's a tragi-comedy from there on.<br />You will never look at your hospital doctor the same way after reading this, but I would recommend you do so, rather than turn up in A &amp;E if you can possibly avoid it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2335549657554641761" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2419319558" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2419319558" />
    <a title="ALLEN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/58158333-allen"><img alt="ALLEN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578421145p2/58158333.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419319558?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ALLEN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ALLEN" href="/user/show/58158333-allen">ALLEN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419319558" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7605940663224301537">A funny, excoriating memoir about a "junior" ob/gyn physician who is "nervous in the service" -- not the military, but Britain's National Health Service during recent years of budget retrenchment, 2004 to 2010. Adam Kay and his colleagues had to deal with weirdly ineffectual decisions coming down the chain-of-command that are spun to send spuriously comforting political messages to the "folks at home" rather than merely save money at all costs. When a volunteer translator renders the Punjabi wor</span>
  <span id="freeText7605940663224301537" style="display:none">A funny, excoriating memoir about a "junior" ob/gyn physician who is "nervous in the service" -- not the military, but Britain's National Health Service during recent years of budget retrenchment, 2004 to 2010. Adam Kay and his colleagues had to deal with weirdly ineffectual decisions coming down the chain-of-command that are spun to send spuriously comforting political messages to the "folks at home" rather than merely save money at all costs. When a volunteer translator renders the Punjabi word indicating a chronic bleeder into "hermaphrodite" rather than "hemophiliac," it's funny but potentially deadly. When an NHS decision from on high takes away the doctors' sleeping cots, remember that your next deliverer of a C-section may have been on his/her feet for 18 hours. God forbid those lazy malingerers should try to stay alert and refreshed! <br /><br />Adam Kay's writing style is funny, but we can see the humor and patience wearing thin when a hemorrhaging patient splashed blood on his scrubs, pants, expensive CK boxers and manhood underneath. The pay these young physicians received for their herculean efforts is usually pitifully small, and once again the invisible bureaucracy seems to have them in their sights--when the docs switch from the Nike type of trainer (athletic) shoes to the much cheaper Crocs, the brass ban use of Crocs but offer no clothing allowances. It's at this point Kay begins to wonder whether the joy of delivering baby after healthy baby really compensates for the occasional heartbreaking failure, the ridiculous hours, low pay, bureaucratic turgidity that ignores success but comes down hard on trivial infractions, and above all the inability to schedule a social life when everyone seems to be slotted in as backup for everyone else. That last problem really hits the fan when time off the author had been promised for a two-week overseas vacation is nullified by a weekend of duty right in the middle. Nobody's fault, but there's no going AWOL. <br /><br />A couple of notes about the language in this highly entertaining memoir with a high "can't-put-it-down" quotient: typically, Kay uses the common four-letter term instead of "manhood" above; Yanks who object to profanity may find the use and frequency of it in this book disconcerting. British slang is freely applied, too, but I forgive him all this for his scrupulousness in footnoting medical terms (which he very much intends to be read), so we readers can understand what references like "trans-vaginal probe" and "pre-eclampsia" and the convoluted acronym "TAH BSO" all mean. <br /><br />We readers know from the introduction to this powerful book that Adam Kay eventually left the National Health Service for a turn at comedy. While the National Health Service does not (yet) subject its patients to American-style five- and six-figure bills, we have to wonder about the priorities of any society that rewards gag-writing for telly so much more handsomely than saving the lives of mothers and fetuses. This shocking (but very funny) black-humored account remains a brisk seller on both sides of the Atlantic. <br /><br /><i>Update: August 31, 2018</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7605940663224301537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10970610598784630370">This was a DNF for me, as a nurse working in the emergency room, I can relate to a lot of the references in this book, especially the dark humour - that’s how we healthcare professionals get through the stress of work.   <span id="freeText10970610598784630370" style="display:none">This was a DNF for me, as a nurse working in the emergency room, I can relate to a lot of the references in this book, especially the dark humour - that’s how we healthcare professionals get through the stress of work. However, I could not stand Kay’s obnoxious views on the struggles doctors deal with day to day, yes being a doctor is relentless, stressful and brings little reward, however he seemed to me to be completely disrespectful of other healthcare professionals and actually quite insulting of midwives in particular. Yes doctors have a difficult time, but so does everyone who works for the NHS, from receptionists, to radiographers, to porters - doctors absolutely do not have the hardest time as he would like you to believe, and it’s not all about them!</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1418580-wendy?shelf=5000-2019">5000-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1418580-wendy?shelf=dec-19">dec-19</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2728129761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1173409550564202953">After reading "This Is Going To Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor" by Adam Kay I have a newfound respect for doctors and nurses.<br/>Adam Kay was a junior doctor from 2004 until 2010 and this is the diary he kept throughout his training. He also added helpful footnotes to explain any medical terms not familiar with readers.<br/>His fascinating account of his life as a doctor was painfully honest, heart-warming and many times hilarious. He explains in great detail his many experiences (including some</span>
  <span id="freeText1173409550564202953" style="display:none">After reading "This Is Going To Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor" by Adam Kay I have a newfound respect for doctors and nurses.<br />Adam Kay was a junior doctor from 2004 until 2010 and this is the diary he kept throughout his training. He also added helpful footnotes to explain any medical terms not familiar with readers.<br />His fascinating account of his life as a doctor was painfully honest, heart-warming and many times hilarious. He explains in great detail his many experiences (including some that made my stomach turn) and the struggles he endured until he got to the point when he made the heart breaking decision to leave his devoted career. Adam's understandable departure from medicine is a great loss to his community and humanity. There are too few doctors with his wit, personality, compassion and devotion.<br />I highly recommend this captivating read!<br /><br />Thank you to NetGalley, author Adam Kay and Little, Brown and Company for an arc of this novel in exchange for my honest review.<br /></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3090957982?book_show_action=true">Dec 18, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paul" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paul" href="/user/show/36511432-paul">Paul</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3090957982" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5399104368320463598">First off I was given a wonderful hard copy of this book by the publisher Little, Brown Spark for an honest review.<br/><br/>Secondly, I have to say I hope I never end up in an english hospital.<br/><br/>This book is a diary and it reads like one. There is no real plot or climax or discovery. We are told from the beginning that the health system in the UK is wonderfully free for all but extremely flawed and most medical staff are overworked to the point of gross negligence. So what we are left with in reading these</span>
  <span id="freeText5399104368320463598" style="display:none">First off I was given a wonderful hard copy of this book by the publisher Little, Brown Spark for an honest review.<br /><br />Secondly, I have to say I hope I never end up in an english hospital.<br /><br />This book is a diary and it reads like one. There is no real plot or climax or discovery. We are told from the beginning that the health system in the UK is wonderfully free for all but extremely flawed and most medical staff are overworked to the point of gross negligence. So what we are left with in reading these daily diary entries are the proof. <br />The entries are mostly written with a sarcastic punch line each one a story within itself. Each entry is well written. Sometimes humorous. Mostly sarcastic. However it is also shocking, disheartening and sad as well. 3 1/2 to 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5399104368320463598" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3138830604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3138830604" />
    <a title="☮Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1076079-karen"><img alt="☮Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605826912p2/1076079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3138830604?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☮Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☮Karen" href="/user/show/1076079-karen">☮Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=5000-2020">5000-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1076079-karen?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3138830604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14898394306633121739">In this book, set in the UK, it is apparent that undergoing medical training under their National Health System reaps huge emotional rewards (I can do great good), but little else in the way of monetary or personal rewards (I most likely will have to work the day of my own wedding/child's Christening/best friend's funeral). Adam Kay's diaries are quite fun and funny, loaded with a unique brand of dark humor I enjoy. Then as long days, derision, and under-staffing take their toll on him, the book</span>
  <span id="freeText14898394306633121739" style="display:none">In this book, set in the UK, it is apparent that undergoing medical training under their National Health System reaps huge emotional rewards (I can do great good), but little else in the way of monetary or personal rewards (I most likely will have to work the day of my own wedding/child's Christening/best friend's funeral). Adam Kay's diaries are quite fun and funny, loaded with a unique brand of dark humor I enjoy. Then as long days, derision, and under-staffing take their toll on him, the book finally takes on a more serious tone and it's really sad how it works out for him and some of his colleagues. I would love to see an American doctor compare his or her experiences with Adam's as I'm sure there are similarities. I do believe UK (junior) doctors struggle with the long hours and low pay a lot longer than in the U.S.<br /><br />A really good book that I recommend.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14898394306633121739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56146790-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529924622p2/56146790.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3149885517?book_show_action=true">Jan 19, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Whitney" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Whitney" href="/user/show/56146790-whitney">Whitney</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3149885517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer787775838243517636">Overall: I loved this one and laughed so many times I lost count. I loved it so much that I read it in a day but it would be a great book to read and put down and come back to often 4/5 or 7.5/10<br/><br/>Summary: <br/>“The difference is obviously the whole ‘life and death’ thing, which is what separates this job from all others, and makes it so unfathomable to people on the outside.” <br/><br/>A collection of diary entries from a junior doctor working in labor and delivery. Some stories are hysterical, some are heartbr</span>
  <span id="freeText787775838243517636" style="display:none">Overall: I loved this one and laughed so many times I lost count. I loved it so much that I read it in a day but it would be a great book to read and put down and come back to often 4/5 or 7.5/10<br /><br />Summary: <br />“The difference is obviously the whole ‘life and death’ thing, which is what separates this job from all others, and makes it so unfathomable to people on the outside.” <br /><br />A collection of diary entries from a junior doctor working in labor and delivery. Some stories are hysterical, some are heartbreaking, but this gives you a great look into what it is like to be a doctor. Highly recommend to anyone interested in medicine or looking for a fun and entertaining read. <br />“So I told them the truth: the hours are terrible, the pay is terrible, the conditions are terrible; you’re underappreciated, unsupported, disrespected and frequently physically endangered. But there’s no better job in the world.” <br /><br />The Good: This book is hysterical and I was laughing through the majority of it. The author has a very dry sense of humor (which I love and found a strength) but some may be uncomfortable with it. It does a great job at helping you understand what doctors got through on a regular basis and it definitely made me empathize with him. <br /><br />“This morning I delivered little baby Sayton – pronounced Satan, as in King of the Underworld.” <br /><br />The Bad: Not much to say here but some may find this offensive. Lots of discussion on genitalia, surgery, blood, sex, and other medical-related themes.<br /><br />Favorite Quotes:<br /><br />“I’m as big a fan of recycling as the next man, but if you turn a used condom inside out and put it back on for round two, it’s probably not going to be that effective.” <br /><br />Today crossed the line from everyday patient idiocy to me checking around the room for hidden cameras. After a lengthy discussion with a patient’s husband about how absolutely no condoms fit him, I establish he’s pulling them right down over his balls. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="787775838243517636" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3207786176" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3207786176" />
    <a title="Dem" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2752994-dem"><img alt="Dem" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1552868566p2/2752994.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3207786176?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dem" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dem" href="/user/show/2752994-dem">Dem</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/35510008-this-is-going-to-hurt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2752994-dem?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3207786176" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18424280609866879335"><b> A series of supposedly funny anecdotes that felt more like a podcast than a novel. </b> <br/> Adam Kay was a junior doctor from 2004 until 2010, before a devastating experience on a ward caused him to reconsider his future. He kept a diary throughout his training, and This Is Going to Hurt intersperses tales from the front line of the NHS with reflections on the current crisis. . <br/>This is one of those books that I keep getting asked about "Did you read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35235302.This_Is_Going_to_Hurt_Secret_Diaries_of_a_Junior_Doctor' title='This Is Going to Hurt Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor by Adam Kay' rel='nofollow noopener'>This Is Going to Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Do</a></span>
  <span id="freeText18424280609866879335" style="display:none"><b> A series of supposedly funny anecdotes that felt more like a podcast than a novel. </b> <br /> Adam Kay was a junior doctor from 2004 until 2010, before a devastating experience on a ward caused him to reconsider his future. He kept a diary throughout his training, and This Is Going to Hurt intersperses tales from the front line of the NHS with reflections on the current crisis. . <br />This is one of those books that I keep getting asked about "Did you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35235302.This_Is_Going_to_Hurt_Secret_Diaries_of_a_Junior_Doctor" title="This Is Going to Hurt Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor by Adam Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Going to Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor</a> and when I answer NO! I am told I have missed out the most amazing book and "you have to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/35235302.This_Is_Going_to_Hurt_Secret_Diaries_of_a_Junior_Doctor" title="This Is Going to Hurt Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor by Adam Kay" rel="nofollow noopener">This Is Going to Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor</a> and now I can confirm I have read it and YES...... It did hurt!<br /><br />I really didnt like the book, it felt contrived and cynical and to be honest full of moaning. I listened to this one on audio and the book was narrated by the author. He spoke quite fast and I I didn’t enjoy the experience.<br /><br />I read 30% and felt that was pretty much as much as I could take. While I didn't enjoy it, it has rave reviews and this review is just my reaction to the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18424280609866879335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PjRsJg3SaNBmjlrl3b9p9aOcA3/o8QxahHns2/7vnhnXc8jdtvT2cRSVRlcUsDJjEKNzuuAI3kmU49oISl2zqw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xYYzgt7z+b5O+ChrwYlEbtIGplrYA503HSN8MdmCL3AswZd5ZdVnHzzjNNkIhh/4YTnWn9D6TyQNuUribTACwg==')})

When his captors discover that he speaks several languages, he is put to work as a Tätowierer (the German word for tattooist), tasked with permanently marking his fellow prisoners.\n\nImprisoned for more than two and a half years, Lale witnesses horrific atrocities and barbarism—but also incredible acts of bravery and compassion. Risking his own life, he uses his privileged position to exchange jewels and money from murdered Jews for food to keep his fellow prisoners alive.\n\nOne day in July 1942, Lale, prisoner 32407, comforts a trembling young woman waiting in line to have the number 34902 tattooed onto her arm. Her name is Gita, and in that first encounter, Lale vows to somehow survive the camp and marry her.\n\nA vivid, harrowing, and ultimately hopeful re-creation of Lale Sokolov\'s experiences as the man who tattooed the arms of thousands of prisoners with what would become one of the most potent symbols of the Holocaust, The Tattooist of Auschwitz is also a testament to the endurance of love and <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10609943895061366598">Adam Kay is an award-winning comedian and writer. He previously worked for many years as a junior doctor. His first book "This is Going to Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor" was a Sunday Times number one bestseller for over a year and has sold over two million copies. It has been translated into 37 languages and is winner of four National Book Awards, including Book of the Year, and will be </span>
  <span id="freeText10609943895061366598" style="display:none">Adam Kay is an award-winning comedian and writer. He previously worked for many years as a junior doctor. His first book "This is Going to Hurt: Secret Diaries of a Junior Doctor" was a Sunday Times number one bestseller for over a year and has sold over two million copies. It has been translated into 37 languages and is winner of four National Book Awards, including Book of the Year, and will be a major new comedy drama for the BBC.<br /><br />His second book "Twas the Nightshift Before Christmas" was an instant Sunday Times number one bestseller and sold over 500,000 copies in its first few weeks.<br /><br />"Dear NHS", edited by Adam Kay, was an instant Sunday Times number one with all profits donated to charity. His first children's book "Kay's Anatomy" will be released in October 2020.</span>
